text:
Made this for dinner last night, what can I say . . .EXCELLENT!  

The only changes I made were I added 1 1/2 tablespoons of lemon juice instead of just 1 tablespoon (this was a recipe for 4) and to be honest, I think next time I will add even more lemon.  We like that lemon flavor!! Also, I used cheddar (hard) slices and I think I will do the shredded cheddar and I will try and spread the cream cheese on (instead of chunky).  Maybe that will prevent it from oozing out!! :) 

Overall, this is an excellent recipe and VERY flavorful and to be honest, VERY easy to make. . .a must try for any household!

text:
Wow - this is fabubous and I swear you could put just about anything rolled up inside a chicken breast and it's bound to be good. Plus the combination of three different cheese was an indication to me that this was going to be tasty. I did make a couple of changes... First I pounded my chicken breasts down thin. Second I used light shredded cheddar cheese that I combined with softened light cream cheese until it was blended. to stuff the chicken and rolled the chicken securing  with toothpicks. I dipped the chicken in egg and milk then the bread crumb mixture to form a light coating. I then drizzled it with the melted butter mixture and baked it according to the directions. The result was a very moist and flavorful chicken bursting with a delicious cheese filled center!

Really good, thanks for sharing.  I actually chose to flatten the chicken, add the cheese and then roll them up.  I used far less cream cheese and threw in some bacon along with the cheese mixture.  Also used Panko crumbs as opposed to breadcrumbs.  I thought the lemon garlic butter was the best thing about this dish, and, if making again, I would ditch dunking them in milk before breading and just use the lemon garlic butter (pouring any remaining over the chicken).  I think that would add tremendous flavor.  Again, thanks for the recipe....it was nice and different!

Yum yum yummy!!! This recipe was so easy - and tastes HEAVENLY! My husband issued appreciative groans (mouth full of warm melted stuffing...) from his side of the plate when this was served! I low-carbed it to my liking - replacing the Italian bread crumbs with almond flour, Italian seasoning, and kosher salt. Also, since I didn't have Romano, I just used more shredded cheddar. This was a heavenly savory recipe  - and great for company! Best of all, I made the full recipe and froze 6 of the chicken breasts. They reheated beautifully as an at-work lunch. What a treat! Thanks for posting this one!

text:
This recipe was excellent!  My husband doesn't care for chicken, so I'm always trying new ways of fixing it.  Well, you know what they say, cheese makes everything taste better!  I butterflied the chicken breasts as directed in the recipe (rather than rolling as suggested by other reviewers) and it worked fine.  Some cheese melted out, but not that much.  I did take the suggestion of reducing the amount of cream cheese.  I reduced it by about a quarter, but I think half would be better next time.  I served this with pasta and we ended up cutting up our chicken breasts into bite size pieces and mixing it with the pasta.  On top of the pasta, I just had a mixture of melted butter, lemon juice, minced garlic and dried basil.  It was delicious!  I will definitely make this again.  It takes a little prepping, but it's worth it.

text:
Delicious and easy! I was looking for a new recipe for chicken, my husband is less than thrilled when I thaw chicken for dinner. Found this one, had everything on hand so I decided to try it. I made just a few changes: I seasoned the chicken with Montreal Chicken seasoning, then used soft cream cheese instead of sliced. I put a dollop inside each breast, and I used shredded cheddar as was suggested by another cook. And it was also suggested to skip the milk, so I did and instead coated the stuffed breasts in the butter/lemon/garlic and then breaded with panko breadcrumbs and parmesan. Drizzled the rest of the butter/lemon sauce over the chicken and baked. So easy, and so tasty! I put this in my recipe box and will definitely be making this one again.

text:
Something very similar but simpler.I started out with the idea of making this according to recipe. I switched it up a bit. I bought two chicken breasts from the meat counter and asked them to butterfly it and tenderize it for me (cut down on the prep time for me). I used presliced mild cheddar and mozzerella cheeses for the filling. This way it would melt more evenly. I also bought a bag of pre shredded Kraft "Italian - Five cheese" cheese for the top. I simply coated the bottom of a cassarole dish with olive oil. Breaded the chicken breasts. Layed one on the bottom (since it was butterflied it was thin and covered the bottom of the whole pan) then ilayered cheeses. Topped that layer with the other breaded chicken breast. Added a little extra bread crumbs on top. Baked at 300 for 20min. Added lemon butter "sauce" and baked another 10 min. Added the Italian -Five cheese mixture to top and baked another 10 min. Chicken was cooked perfect and was absolutely delicious and alot easier than messing around with toothpicking or rolling the chicken. I made twice as much of the lemon butter suace and mixed it in with bowtie pasta. Worked perfect and tied everything together. I will be making it over and over again. The boyfriend already wants it again next week. Absolutely amazing!

text:
Very good chicken recipe!!  I halved the recipe using 3 large chicken breasts and butterflied as the recipe directed (rather than pounding as others suggested) and it worked fine.  I used 1/3 less fat cream cheese and just spread a thin layer across the entire piece of chicken then topped with shredded Colby jack cheese and crumbled bacon.  I would HIGHLY RECOMMEND THE BACON, it added a lot of flavor and took away from the richness of all the cheese (also great for low carb diet)!  Cooked about 40 minutes and served with rice and salad.

text:
Unbelievably good!  However, I did make a few changes.  Instead of sliced cheeses, I mixed shredded cheddar cheese with a block of cream cheese then divided it evenly between the breasts (much easier to handle this way!).  In addition, I added a couple stalks of asparagus to each chicken roll.  The contrast between the crunch of the asparagus and the creaminess of the cheese was to die for!  Then instead of dipping my chicken roll into milk, I dipped each roll into melted butter instead (1/2 cup...it's not like this recipe is low fat).  I skipped the lemon/butter sauce and baked it as is.  Then I topped with Blender Hollandaise Sauce from this site.  My husband wants to to make this for our next dinner party, it is THAT good!

text:
This was a really easy recipe that tastes like you slaved away all day. I used 6 breasts cause that's all I had. I also had half of a pack (4oz) of fat-free cream cheese and some shredded cheddar cheese left over from another recipe so I just divided the cream cheese in 6 equal slices and placed inside the sliced breast as the recipe describes.I then eye balled the cheddar and used it up equally. I used a prepackaged breading mix so I dipped the breasts in melted butter then into the breading. Using the same butter, I then added the garlic and lemon juice and let the garlic cook a little bit then drizzled it over the chicken. Mine took about 50 mintues to bake in the 350 degree oven. I got no oozing of the cheese and the breasts were tender and juicy and delicious.

Very nice and rich! Everyone liked this, even my picky eater. We halved the recipe and had to make our own seasoned bread crumbs with Panko crumbs and Italian herb seasoning blend (what was in the house) and I think the Panko crumbs give an excellent crunch. The store was out of Romano cheese so I subbed Parmesan. I think the Romano would have been better though. Used just under half the melted butter with 1 TBSP lemon juice, but next time I would used the 2 TBSP even for half the recipe. I like it a tad more lemony because the chicken is so rich. Definitely season the chicken with the garlic salt and paprika. Next time I would add some pepper too. We cooked it a little more than the time said because the chicken was still pink. Served with bow-tie pasta and pesto, and salad.

text:
I made this tonight for dinner, and my family loved it. I halved the recipe using 4 chicken breasts. The only changes were to accommodate personal tastes and ingredients I had on-hand. The breasts were very large. So I increased the bread crumbs and added Kraft Oven Fry for more crunch. I used fresh shredded parmigiano reggiano instead of Romano cheese because that's what I had on hand, and increased the garlic and lemon juice a little for the butter sauce. I pounded the breasts before cutting the pockets, and baked them for 40 minutes because they were so large. 3 of us ate only two of the breasts with mixed rice and Normandy veggies, and we were all stuffed. Prep took me about 30 minutes and cook time 40 minutes. The finished dish looked, smelled, and tasted wonderful. It was very rich will all of the cheese, and not something you would want to eat too often. As a special treat or an elegant looking meal to serve guests, this would be perfect. When making it, choose small breast for each person to have a whole one, or plan on 1/2 breast for each person. This recipe also opens a whole realm of ideas for different stuffings.

text:
Just tried this recipe for the first time and made some modification based on everyone's input and I made it for 6 servings. It turned out fantastic! I cut the lemon garlic butter sauce with olive oil and used the "smart balance" 50/50 buttery spread to cut the fat content a bit. I also added fresh ground 3 pepper blend and a bit of cayenne pepper (1/4 tsp)for the sauce; extra lemon juice (about 3 1/2 tbsp of lemon juice). 

For the stuffing I used 1 cup of shredded mozzarella cheese and 1/2 cup of shredded colby jack cheese. I also took another reviewers advice and used sour cream (light sour cream) instead of the cream cheese. About 3/4 cup of light sour cream. I mixed the cheeses and sour cream together in a big bowl and added 1/2 of a diced red onion and 1/2 of each of red, yellow and orange bell peppers chopped as well. (fresh and ground salt pepper to taste!)

I butterflied the breasts and used toothpicks to secure it (didn't pound the meat). I then dipped them in non fat milk and then to the bread crumb mix.

Used an Italian bread crumb mix and added cayenne pepper (about 1/2-3/4 tsp) and mixed it all together with about a 1/2 a cup of grated Parmesan and Romano cheese.

I noted that a couple people mentioned the chicken was soggy on the bottom so I baked it on a cookie drying rack on top of a baking sheet (to catch the run off).

It was perfectly cooked in 30 min and is about the best this I've ever made. Thank you for the initial recipe and for everyone's suggestions

text:
Very enjoyable dish! My husband said it tasted "gourmet". I do have a few suggestions though. First, definitely, season the chicken breast itself with salt, pepper, and whatever other herbs or spices that you like. In addition, I would also season the bread crumb and romano (I used parmesan) mixture with a small amount of, again, whatever you like. I used very small amounts of onion powder, oregano, and basil on both the chicken and in the bread crumb mixture. Secondly, as other reviewers suggested, I pounded the chicken breasts, put in the cream cheese and cheddar, rolled it up, and secured it with toothpicks. Since the breats are thinner they cook faster, so keep an eye on them. This really was moist and flavorful chicken. The cream cheese and cheddar sounds strange together, but it was terrific. Next time I am going to try an herbed cream cheese!

text:
I've made this several times according to the recipe and it's good, but the last time I drifted a bit and it became phenomenal. For the garlic butter sauce I kept the butter at the original amount but doubled the garlic and lemon to bring out more of the flavors, and I was out of cheddar cheese at the time so I substituted it for pepper jack cheese slices with whipped cream cheese with 2 green onions added to the mix. The taste was so good that my husband has asked for it several times. The pepper jack and green onions really give it a more dynamic flavor along with the tanginess of the lemon.

Truly Amazing! This has replaced my whole family's favorite dish, even my 5 yr old LOVED it! I did however change a few things like other reviewers suggested. I only used 3oz of cream cheese and I added an extra tablespoon of lemon juice. I cut the milk in half and added two eggs and beat it all together. I also used chicken tenderloins and beat them flat and rolled it I held them together with toothpicks. I thought the butter mixture would be too much but I wasn't. I did however pour half on top before cooking and mid way through I coated the chicken rolls with the remainder of the butter mixture. Loved loved loved this recipe! I will be making this quite often.

text:
I enjoyed this recipe but I did make some changes: I used thin sliced chicken breasts because I never have any luck trying to butterfly the thicker ones.  I pound them a little thinner if need be and place the filling in the middle and roll in both sides.  I filled with creamcheese and a slice of sharp chedder.  I wrapped each piece of chicken in bacon instead of breading them which was sufficient enough to keep the breasts closed.  Halfway through the baking process I poured the butter lemon mixture over the top.  At the very end, I broiled them for a few minutes to brown and crisp the bacon.  Delish!

text:
Husband proclaimed this delicious, so thank you, thank you, thank you!  My tweaks:  like others, I used panko, mixing in a generous amount of Italian herb seasoning and Romano cheese.  When coating chicken, I always line my baking pan with foil and spray a rack with Pam, cooking the chicken above the foil.  Makes top and bottom crust nice and crunchy.  I used cream cheese and smoked mozzarella, smooshing the cheeses over the meat until it went almost to the edge.  After dipping in milk and dredging, I sprinkled the remaining crumbs over the top.  Went light with the butter, with more lemon juice, and seasoned with garlic salt, pepper and paprika.  The chicen was pretty thick, so I roasted at 400* (convection) for 30 minutes, and it turned out perfectly.  Husband and I are both cheese fanatics, so I can see endless possibilities!

text:
This recipe is good and I love the idea/concept behind it. I was more or so looking for a base recipe for some stuffed chicken. I hate when people change the recipe, so I did try it as per recipe except for pounding and rolling the chicken instead of bookstyle and it was okay. There was something missing with the filling. The breading was great. What would make the recipe awesome, would be to soften the creamcheese a little and add shredded cheddar, some garlic salt (needs salt!!). Mix the filling together and the add to the chicken. Most of my cheddar came out and left just the cream cheese- which seemed bland since there were no seasonings at all inside, all of it is for the breading! Great starter recipe, to add new things and try your own variations.

text:
5 star! Higher if I could rate it! I cut the recipe in half, but used 5 smaller breast, rather than the called for 4. Pounded them flat and then rolled them and secured with toothpicks, rather than butterflying and stuffing. Used only 3 oz of cream cheese (1/3 less fat) cut into 5 slices. Used less than the mentioned cheddar cheese too, and used shredded cheese.  Just filled until I thought they were full, didnt really measure. Used homemade bread crumbs from the Garlic Bread recipe on this site and added a few shakes of italian seasoning.  Used fresh grated parmesan cheese rather than ramano since that was what I had on hand. Used a little extra lemon and 2 tsp garlic in sauce. Baked at 350 for 40 minutes, then put under high broiler for 2 minutes to crispen top. Amazing recipe! WIll make again for sure. Thanks!

I decided to rate this recipe on the way that it was written.  i gave it four stars because my guests and I both believed there was to much garlic (over powered the lemon) and cheese. I will definitely make it again.

If I could rate highly than 5, I would!  This is Heavenly!  I changed the recipe slightly.  I didn't have any minced garlic so i used some minced onion and garlic powder.  I did not measure the lemon juice I just poured some in the pan (I love lemon flavor!).  I used the thick boneless, skinless chicken breasts and cut a slit in each; put the cream cheese and cheddar cheese slices inside the chicken and used toothpicks to hold it shut.  I dipped it in the milk and breadcrumbs and then poured the garlic, onion, lemon mixed over top the chicken in the baking pan.  I cooked it for 45 minutes and IT IS WONDERFUL! Thanks for the great recipe, I will definately be making this again many times!

text:
I made the recipe as directed- the only thing I modified was the oven temp and cooking time. I cooked at 450 degrees for 20-22 minutes. It came out perfectly juicy and browned on the top. I upped the degrees because you are pouring lemon and butter sauce on top of chicken coated in parm and breadcrumbs...in my experience, if you cook on too low of heat, you get soggy coating.
One thing I would change in the future is just a tad more seasoning...probably just add some extra salt on top of chicken in addition to what recipe calls for. Otherwise, this was a huge hit at our house and super easy!

text:
I have to confess that I let my imagination run amok.  I used boneless, skinless chicken thighs because I had them on hand.  Instead of cream cheese, I laid the thighs open, seasoned the inside of each with S, P, and a little garlic powder, then placed half a slice of ham off the bone on each, followed by a slice of swiss cheese, and followed that with a half slice of sharp cheddar.  I then rolled up each thigh (no toothpick required) and placed them seam side down in a pre-sprayed quiche dish, seasoned the outsides as I did the insides, did the melted butter/lemon juice on each, followed by garlic and herb bread crumbs and baked 25 mins at 350.  I pulled the dish out, laid a half slice of swiss on top of each thigh, then back into the oven for about 4-5 mins until cheese was melted.  OH, SO GOOD!!!!!!

text:
This is a phenomenal recipe.
My husband now BEGS ME for this for every occasion...
"Honey it's a Tuesday, that means stuffed chicken!"
I used this exact recipe once, now I've been following my own version of it for a while now.
It's a good bit of prepping- but what I don't think many people realize is that it actually FREEZES well! I just ate one a frozen and cooked for an hour earlier!

I buy my chicken, butterfly open (or buy thin and roll and hold with tooth picks)

In a separate bowl I mix 1 block of cream cheese and half a bag of shredded cheddar cheese.

In another separate bowl I have milk, then in another I have Italian Bread Crumbs.

I stuff, dunk in milk, roll in bread crumbs then lay on a pan.

I squeeze fresh lemons and mix fresh grated pepper in it.

I then drizzle the dressing over the chicken breast.
Then I add a few sprinkles of garlic salt and paprika over it.

The recipe she listed is PHENOMENAL! And I've used it for so long, ^ above is just what it's turned into now.

text:
This was very delicious! Like everyone else, I made several changes. I only stuffed it with Mild cheddar to cut the calories from using both cheeses. Salted the inside and outside of the chicken and seasoned the inside with a season mix. From past experiences, if you don't season and salt it comes out very bland. I didn't have milk so I coated my chicken with eggs and added grated parm to my italian bread crumbs. Opted out on the butter with garlic to cut down on calories. I love lemons so after the chicken was almost done cooking I drizzled fresh lemon juice over it. My chicken came out golden and crispy and very moist. Great base recipe.

text:
As noted by other reviewers, cut down the portions! I used about 1/2 of the 8 oz cream cheese between 3 large breasts, and I did use mild shredded cheddar only I cut my breast partially in half from the back then cut the breasts open from the middle so the back was kind of like a pair of doors. I found the cream cheese stayed inside the chicken very well but the cheddar did not. The next time I try this I will also put some cheddar in first, then the cream cheese, then a layer of cheddar so that if the bottom layer falls out again, at least there will be one of the cheddar and the cream cheese. 

ALSO, YOU DO NOT NEED SO MUCH BUTTER! OH MY GOSH! NO! I cut the butter to 1/2 a cup and that was too much! I will only use a quarter next time. I also used half of a lemon, I didn't even measure but I didn't taste it much so I will just chalk it up to the whole thing next time. Also we love garlic so I put in more than what it asked for and the garlic didn't burn and actually tasted really nicely coarsely chopped on top of the chicken.

Aside from making this recipe not so much of an artery blocker, it was really delicious! It was simple and my family loved it.

text:
Normally anything is 3/4 c of butter doesn't get a second look from me but I decided to lighten up this recipe and it turned out great.  Here's how:
* Use cooking spray to "grease" the pan
* Use reduced fat (1/3 less) cream cheese rather than full fat
* Use 2% shredded cheese (I used Colby Jack because that's what I had)
* Skip dunking the breasts in milk.  If you haven't dried them, they will be moist enough to dredge in bread crumbs and cheese.
* Drizzle lemon juice (I probably used 2 T for 2 breasts) directly on to breasts (skipping the butter altogether), then sprinkle garlic and paprika directly on the breasts in the pan.

text:
My whole family loved this recipe, and believe me finding a recipe that everyone in my family loves is a task unto itself. 

I made a few adjustments though, and they are: 

Instead of Italian Bread Crumbs I used Panko, Japanese Style Bread Crumbs, Plain.

For the Cheddar Cheese I used Cabot's Seriously Sharp Cheddar and of Course, Philadelphia Cream Cheese. I used Bel Gioioso Freshly Shredded Romano Cheese to add to the Panko. 

The Recipe called for baking for 30 minutes, but the breasts I used were rather thick and still slightly frozen in the center, so my baking time was about an hour. Well worth the wait though, it was perfect.

I also made the Country Apple Dumplings for dessert that night, it was the perfect ending to a perfect meal.

This was pretty good!  I do agree with others the the cream cheese could be reduced and next time I make it I will reduce the cream cheese maybe by alittle less than half.  As far as the chicken breasts, they vary so much in size anymore.  I had 3 chicken breasts from SAMs to totaling 2.5lbs.  I certainly was not going to use eight of those! if I would have used eight of those giant breasts perhaps there wouldn't have been too much cream cheese.   I sliced the chicken breasts in half to make 6 peices and then pounded them thin enough to fold up with the cheeses.  My brests fit snugly in a 9x13 dish, which I think helped to keep the cheeses in.  Over all a good recipe!

text:
This tastes a lot like Ruth's Chris Steakhouse stuffed chicken!  I cut off any fat, then butterfly and flatten the chicken with a meat pounder.  Put the cream cheese in the microwave for 20 seconds or so just until it is spreadable and spread evenly on the chicken. Season the chicken with a little dried rosemary and garlic powder.  Then I sprinkle on shredded cheddar cheese, roll the chicken up and secure with 3 toothpicks before dipping in milk and breading (this keeps the cheese inside!).  I do use extra lemon juice - about 4 - 6 TBS.  Everyone loved this including my 11 year old brother, he requested this for Thanksgiving!  It is a little time consuming, but it is worth it!

I've made this twice so far, revising a little the second time to my family's liking. Firstly, I only had frozen chicken breast tenderloins, but that actually turns out better for me because it's easier to make more portions and fit it in my baking dish. I pounded the thawed chicken flat, and rolled it. I spread the cream cheese (as well as using less of it, my brother isn't fond of cream cheese) and instead of using Cheddar, I used ColbyJack cheese. I usually serve it with mashed potatoes and steamed brocolli.

This was very delicious. I softened my cream cheese and mixed in some grated cheddar before stuffing the chicken with it instead of using slices of each. This recipe was good, but i made some modifications due to lack of ingredients i had at home. I pounded the chicken to about 1/4" thick and spread a layer of cream cheese. text:
This chicken is great. You can modify the filling to suit your own tastes and mood of the day. I used about half of the cream cheese that was called for and found that to be perfect. I added 1/2 Tbls of minced garlic to 1 cup melted butter and 8tsp lemon juice to make the lemon butter mixture for 6 chicken breasts. After the cheddar cheese and cream cheese were placed on the chicken, I sprinkled the inside of the chicken with paprika, garlic salt and drizzled with a bit of the lemon butter mixture.I dipped the chicken in the lemon butter before breading (omitted the milk).  I did have to raise the oven temperature to 375 and bake for 45 minutes. This is a definite keeper, CHRCAMILLO! Thank you for posting the recipe.

Otherwise, you might want to omit one or the other of the cheeses, or at least cut back on the cream cheese and I would only use Extra Sharp cheddar for this. The rest of the recipe was AWESOME once you got over the richness of the stuffing. Even my partner who I have to hide cheese from so I know its there for recipes, thought that the chesse was a little overwhelming.

This was such a fancy but simple recipe.  I only made three pieces of chicken for us.  I made slight changes - since I am on Weight Watchers, I used fat free cream cheese and Kraft 2% Sharp Cheddar for the filling and mixed the bread crumbs with Kraft Lite Parmesan cheese. I had to bake it for 50 minutes though - maybe my chicken pieces were too big?  Regardless, this is a HUGE hit with us and it will stay in my file.  This will be what I make the next time I have company.

text:
I am glad to have found this recipe, it was great!  I made just two half breasts with this recipe, adjusting ingredients accordingly.  I used garlic pam-type spray instead of oil.  I only used about 1 1/2 - 2 tsp cream cheese per breast half, it was plenty rich enough in flavor.  I also added a little pepper, some SpiceHunter Garlic Pepper Blend, and just a little seasoning salt to the inside of the chicken.  I cut down on the butter and increased the garlic to drizzle on the top.  I appreciate the tip from another reader about the French Fried onions, I'll try that next time.  Our opinion is:  More garlic - more lemon juice.  Maybe try Meyer lemon juice for a little different flavor some time.  GREAT recipe, we THANK you!

text:
YUMMY!!!! This was a wonderful combination of different tastes that came together to complement one another! I must confess that we did not enjoy the garlic salt and felt that it competed with the rest of the dish; I won't use that again. I will use only half of the cream cheese next time, and I may use shredded cheddar cheese for ease of placement within the butterflied chicken breast. Everyone has their own techniques! We halved the recipe but did not halve the garlic lemon butter sauce; I think I will double that next time; we just loved it! I used the asiago-romano-parmesan cheese from Kraft and this was delicious with the italian bread crumbs. Please give this recipe a try; it is just delicious and a nice change to chicken. You can use reduced fat cheese and fat free cream cheese to improve the healthiness of this dish. Enjoy! Mmmm, my mouth is watering just thinking about this chicken!

I made this last night and it turned out very tasty. For some reason the milk did not act as a good binder for the bread crumbs. Not a problem, though. After I drizzled the butter mixture, I added more bread crumbs on top of the chicken. I might use an egg or half and half next time. Another difference I used was whipped cream cheese (I figured spreading it would do better). I added just enough garlic salt to the cream cheese to give it some flavor. By using the whipped cream cheese, my blocks of cheddar stayed inside the chicken better. Leftovers were even better the next night! This is a wonderful recipe.

This was an excellent new dish that I made for guests over the weekend, and it just became my wife's new favorite dish. In fact, she's  enjoying the leftovers now.

A few tweaks I recommend:
- You can use about 1/2 the amount of milk.
- You'll have a lot of breadcrumbs left over. Just throw them into the chicken folds. They add to the stuffing.
- I expected the cream cheese to melt and blend in with the cheddar, but it didn't. Next time my cream cheese slices will be 1/4" or less.

text:
Made this about 5 times now and my kids say it's their new fave.  They ask me to make it every week.  If you follow the recipe exactly it's amazing but you can make small tweaks to your taste and it's still amazing.  We like lemon so I use one extra table spoon of lemon and I use whatever breadcrumbs I have in my pantry - Italian, garlic, it all tastes great.  I grate my cheddar cheese and always use green onion cream cheese (adds the best flavor).  I mix the grated cheddar and cream cheese together and put spoonfuls into the butterflied breasts.  Yes, the cheese melts out in the pan a bit but my family says this is the best part and spoons it over rice.  Really solid awesome recipe that is now one of my standard rotations.

text:
Because I didn't exactly follow the recipe I almost didn't review it, but then I thought that I wasn't the only one caught with my dilemma as I prepared this for two of us.  I was ready with the milk and do the breadcrumbs when I discovered that I was out of breadcrumbs.  What to do?!  So I mixed the butter sauce, put the cheeses inside the chicken breasts as called for by the submitter using toothpicks to hold them together, and put them in a small very heavy saucepan with the butter.  I covered the chicken breasts with parmesan.  I cooked them on stovetop with the lid for about 20 minutes on a very low setting and then without the lid for the final part until they were done according to my Thermapen.  They were delicious!  I would definitely do this again just exactly this way!  This was not only easy but very delicious!  Thank you so much, CHRCAMILLO!

text:
This was good, but I too found the cooking time a little off.  I think it depends on how thick your chicken breasts are, so I had to add another 10 minutes to be on the safe side.  I butterflied the breasts, and spread a good hunk of softened cream cheese on the chicken breast then added shredded sharp cheddar. I closed it by placing several toothpicks on the seam.  Did not have any problems with leaking cheese.  Next time I make this, I think that I will had some chopped green onions to the cream cheese and use garlic salt instead of the minced garlic and maybe more lemon.  The garlic was not very pronounced, neither was the lemon.  This would even be delicious with blue cheese.  Overall a good recipe you can have fun with using your own ideas.  Thinly sliced ham would also be great in this.  Thank you for sharing this recipe.  I will definitely make this again.

text:
This recipe was good enough for me to serve to 80 people for a Sunday School class dinner!  The modifications I made to feed the crowd were:  pounded chicken day before, added garlic and italian seasonings to cream cheese mixture, used shredded cheddar, added egg to milk.  I rolled chicken up, didn't even use toothpicks-only minor leakage!  I assembled chicken rolls early in day, then just drizzled with sauce and baked right before serving.  Did have to re-pan after cooking, quite a bit of grease with butter sauce and cheese stuffing, so for presentation I put into clean pan for buffet.  Served with roasted asparagus and red potatoes with rosemary.  Guests absolutely loved it!!

text:
Amazing recipe.  When you thought there were no other ways to prepare baked chicken.  The cream cheese/cheddar cheese blend is what makes this recipe work.  Even if you dont like cream cheese alone, it takes on a new taste when melted and blended.  Use good quality cheddar, like Tillamook sharp cheddar.  I also suggest using the optional paprika, as the color jazzes up the appearance on the plate.  Can cut the fat a bit by using lower fat cheese. 

Will be making often.

The garlic-lemon-butter sauce really made this recipe. I doubled the amount so I had more to pour over the chicken after it was done. Yum! I did do like others suggested and pounded the chicken breasts then rolled them up and secured with toothpicks -- it made them very elegant looking. Good recipe! Everyone loved it. Great blend of flavors! I used Italian flavored shake & bake for chicken mixed with freshly shredded parmesan , 2 LARGE cloves of garlic and 2 tlbs. of lemon juice with the butter. text:
We loved this.  Prep took me longer than stated, however. My chicken breasts, I guess, were thinner than normal;I had a terrible time cutting the breast "pockets,(and I have done before) so after 4 trys I rolled up like other reviewers.  I did use the paprika on top to add some color for presentation. I did not use the garlic salt as I thought the butter would make it salty enough. We loved the mix of cheddar and cream cheese with the garlic/butter sauce. It is rich, but not as rich as an Alfredo.  Separately, I cooked brocolli flowerettes and added to a platter with the chicken. Presentation was five star also, with the green brocolli.  Will make this for company as I think almost everyone would like this. Great recipe!
